Sawlogs . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . 38 of Sveaskog‚Äôs sustainability reporting . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . The sustainability report comprises pages 16‚Äì17, 25‚Äì35, 48‚Äì53, 119‚Äì125. Sweden‚Äôs biggest forest owner Sveaskog is Sweden‚Äôs biggest forest owner and is owned by the Swedish state. The company owns 14 per cent of Sweden‚Äôs forest land, has operations in 170 municipalities and has 840 employees. Sveaskog conducts forestry and trade activities with wood raw materials in Sweden. Its main products are saw logs, pulpwood and chips as well as biofuel. Sveaskog‚Äôs customers are primarily located in Sweden and in the forest industry. The Swedish forest industry is export-oriented and delivers to markets all over the world. Activities Good demand in brief The biggest market for the Swedish forest industry when it comes to pulp, 100% paper and sawn wood products is Europe including Sweden. However, global demand trends for these products are important to the Swedish state-owned forest industry. The state of the market has been very good during the year and has also beneÔ¨Åted from a favourable exchange rate for Swedish companies. Despite some fall in demand and prices during the latter part of the year, the state of the market is still good and prices are favourable for forest products, not least measured in Swedish kronor. Fluctuations in exchange rates continue to have a signiÔ¨Åcant impact on the proÔ¨Åtability of the Swedish forest industry. Sweden‚Äôs biggest forest owner The availability of wood raw materials has, due to weather disturbances in the form of a lot of snow during the winter and spring and the dry summer, had an adverse effect on industrial production. In addition, the availability of felling and transport resources during the year has limited the supply capacity from the forest. 840 employees Sveaskog combines proÔ¨Åtable forestry with the preservation of high natural values. The company decided as early as in 2002 to invest in long-term 37 ecoparks conservation corresponding to 20 per cent of its productive forest land, and during 2018 Sveaskog‚Äôs ecoparks celebrated their Ô¨Åfteenth anniversary. The Ô¨Årst was opened in 2003 and there are now 37 ecoparks in total. Sveaskog also has a very strong focus on innovation issues. The development efforts are focused on increasing timber production and productivity in forestry, reducing costs and environmental impact, and ensuring better use of and increasing the value of wood raw materials and forest land. Owns 14% of Sweden‚Äôs forest land 6,971 million SEK net revenue KEY FIG U R ES 2018 in brief Sveaskog‚Äôs operating proÔ¨Åt for the year as a whole is the best it has ever been. Net sales, which include both deliveries from Sveaskog‚Äôs own forest and externally sourced wood raw materials, increased by 12 per cent to SEK 6,971 million (6,206). The prices increased by 11 per cent on average and the total delivery volumes increased by one per cent. Operating proÔ¨Åt increased by 14 per cent and amounted to SEK 1,422 million (1,248). The positive effect of higher prices has been somewhat counteracted by four per cent lower delivery volumes from Sveaskog‚Äôs own forests, where the margins are higher than for externally sourced wood raw materials. Costs related to forest Ô¨Åres and reduced sales of non-forest land have had a negative effect on proÔ¨Åt. Very good proÔ¨Åt from activities combined with a strong capital structure enables the Board to propose increasing the dividend to SEK 1,100 million (900) to the annual general meeting. During 2018, Sveaskog was the Ô¨Årst forest products company in Sweden to quantify all the values of the forest. This Unique work aims to promote everything the forest has to offer and show how many more values there are in addition to what we previously reported in the Ô¨Ånancial result. The idea is not to commercialise these values, but to provide insight into our impact, whether positive or negative. Through this work, we have managed to quantify carbon sequestration, recreation, hunting and berry picking as well as Ô¨Ånancial values such as taxes and other contributions to the community, among other things. Stockholm in March 2019 In the long term, we also want to show how strategic choices affect forest values. For example, when we choose to increase growth through fertilisation, we know that the forest will grow faster and sequester even more carbon dioxide. But we also know that fertilisation can affect the natural values. Sveaskog creates many values. These include economic, social and environmental values. In addition to the Ô¨Ånancial result, Sveaskog‚Äôs forests contribute to solving the climate challenge since the forestry sequesters carbon dioxide. You can read about Sveaskog‚Äôs value creation on the following pages. A N N UA L A N D S U S TA I N A B I LI T Y R E P O R T, 2 018 11 VALU E CR EATION The forest Sveaskog uses the forest with the aim of combining economic, ecological and social considerations. More biomass and more biodiversity need to be created so that the values for future generations are strengthened. S veaskog aims to be a leader within sustainable forestry. This is done through active, proÔ¨Åtable and responsible use of forests and land to ensure and increase growth on a continuous basis, to enrich nature and to create value for future generations. In 2018, Sveaskog delivered 11 million cubic metres of sawlogs, pulpwood and biofuel to customers while also increasing the biodiversity of its own forests. Forests form the basis of the Swedish bioeconomy. To meet customers‚Äô demand for different qualities and volumes, Sveaskog supplies raw materials from its own forests and from other forest owners in Sweden and abroad. More growth than felling The forest must be used Each year, Sveaskog thins or clearcuts approximately today, but it must also be 50,000 hectares. The felling levels are optimised in preserved for future generations. the long term so that they do not have to be lowered in the future, thereby ensuring stability for Sveaskog in both deliveries and proÔ¨Åtability. Sveaskog works with 100-year plans. There is more growth than felling in the forest. In 2018, 70 per cent of the growth Increased growth on managed land was felled. A N N UA L A N D S U S TA I N A B I LI T Y R E P O R T, 2 018 13 EXTE R NAL FACTORS External aÔ¨Äecting Sveaskog‚Äôs activities factors Climate change Global climate agreement COP 21 describes the sustainable use of forests as a key factor for ensuring that the temperature of the Earth does not increase more than two degrees. With active and sustainable forestry, we can keep using the growing forest and wood raw materials to replace products based on fossil raw materials. The green transition and wood as a material The growing forest sequesters carbon dioxide and the DIGITALISATION wood raw materials can in turn replace fossil products and their manufacturing processes. There is a risk that world trade will develop in a negative direction, even though there are a lot of positive economic signals just now. However, the development of many of the leading world markets is difÔ¨Åcult to assess, Views of the forest such as how Brexit might affect the signiÔ¨Åcant British demand. The discussion of what the forest is to be used for and what sustainable forestry means is intensifying. There is also increasing polarisation of views on preserving forests on the one hands and using them on the other. In the spring of 2018, the government decided on a strateTransparency gy for Sweden‚Äôs national forest programme, after which regional forest programmes were developed. The nationIn the discussions concerning, among other things, al forest programme is an important basis for choosing how forestry affects biodiversity, transparency requirefocus areas and coming up with sustainable strategies. ments are increasing. During 2018, Sveaskog graduThe heart of the entire programme is the broad dialogue ally published the natural value assessments that are on the role of forests in a sustainable society and growing always carried out before plans are made to fell trees bioeconomy. in an area. This was done to increase transparency and improve dialogue with those who want insight into the assessments. Skills provision and forest knowledge Urbanisation means that forest knowledge in Swedish society is in danger of diminishing. Fewer and fewer Swedes will thus have direct experience of forestry. At the same time, there is a growing interest in what the forest offers in the form of renewable raw materials, climate beneÔ¨Åts and experiences as well as biodiversity. A general challenge that the forestry industry will face in the future is the rural Ô¨Çight, which may make it more difÔ¨Åcult to Ô¨Ånd the right skills. COLLABORATION AND DIALOGUE Sveaskog is a company at the heart of society and has activities in 170 of the country‚Äôs 290 municipalities. The forest affects and interests people. That is why Sveaskog has a close stakeholder dialogue with many different players. Such players include municipalities, private individuals, non-proÔ¨Åt organisations such as cooperative associations, conservation organisations, sports clubs or nature tourism enterprises. Sveaskog also consults with the S√°mi communities, as there may be conÔ¨Çicts of interest between reindeer husbandry and felling activities. A N N UA L A N D S U S TA I N A B I LI T Y R E P O R T, 2 018 15 M U LTI DI M E NSIONAL VALU E CR EATION Sveaskog‚Äôs sustainable value chain Sveaskog uses the forest and makes a proÔ¨Åt through sales. But other values are also created through the forest holdings and use of the forests. Sveaskog is the Ô¨Årst forest products company in Sweden to use the IP&L method, which is a unique way of measuring hidden values that exist, but have not been measured before, such as recreation. We developed this method in 2018, together with world-leading sustainability economist Pavan Sukhdev. Clearing Clearing entails thinning out the forest stand so that the most suitable trees have the space to grow and development. Thinning Thinning improves the quality of the remaining trees. Tree trunks taken out during thinning are mainly used for pulpwood, but also for sawlogs and bioenergy. Final felling During final felling, Sveaskog mainly fells trees for sawlogs and a smaller proportion for pulpwood. ... creates value for the customers Sawmills Sveaskog supplies sawlogs to sawmills in Sweden. This is guided by the UN‚Äôs 2030 Agenda for Sustainable Development and the 17 Sustainable Development Goals. Sveaskog‚Äôs priorities are also inÔ¨Çuenced by the structured dialogue with company stakeholders. Their opinions play an important role in the materiality analysis that forms the basis of Sveaskog‚Äôs priorities and strategic approaches to sustainability. This includes both views from the stakeholder dialogue and Sveaskog‚Äôs own view of which issues are of greatest importance. E ach year, Sveaskog carries out a materiality analysis in which the most important issues from a sustainability perspective are listed. These are the sustainability issues that have the greatest impact on Sveaskog, but also the issues that Sveaskog is best able to inÔ¨Çuence as a company. Stakeholder perceptions are based on a number of index measurements with detailed questions directed at different groups: employees, customers and local organisations. The opinions of stakeholders are then compiled and the various issues discussed by Sveaskog‚Äôs sustainability committee and Sveaskog‚Äôs group management. During 2018, the weighting of a number of issues was increased in the analysis. This includes the importance of game conservation in relation to the local hunting laws to deal with damage caused by elk grazing. Another issue is skills development and meeting new knowledge needs has an impact on areas that are important to reindeer among stakeholders when it comes to the changes that the husbandry. Both the forestry and reindeer husbandry forestry industry is undergoing. Sweden will lead the way in implementing the agenda with a transition both at home and in the global system, according to the government‚Äôs national action plan for the 2030 Agenda. Industry plays a crucial role in achieving the goals, and Sveaskog has accepted this task in earnest. Sveaskog can relate to all of the goals, but has mapped those where the company can contribute in the most relevant way. Sveaskog has also carried out an analysis of its value creation and the added value generated by its activities and forest assets. Goal 5: Achieve gender equality Goal 11: Sustainable cities and empower all women and girls and communities With increased gender equality There are an increasing number of and diversity, the recruitment base solutions for building larger and higher is broadened and the future skills structures using wood, and Sveaskog has provision improved. identiÔ¨Åed partnerships within the timber construction industry as a focus area for future development. Goal 8: Decent work and Goal 13: Climate action economic growth Forests absorb carbon dioxide, and a Sveaskog‚Äôs activities contribute to growing forest can absorb even more. a vibrant countryside and economic Sveaskog is working actively to reduce growth outside of large towns and dependence on fossil energy sources cities. Employees of SIA Sveaskog Baltfor are not included. 2) Work-related injuries: accidents, accidents on way to and from work, work-related illnesses that at the time of reporting are considered to have led to the absence. Also includes minor injuries at Ô¨Årst aid level. Contractors‚Äô work-related injuries are not included in this data. Work-related injuries are recorded using the SKIA tool. SKIA is the forestry industry‚Äôs information system on the work environment and is provided to the industry by AFA Insurance. Any work-related injuries at Baltfor are not recorded in SKIA and are thus not included in the calculation. However, the average number of employees includes employees at Baltfor. Accidents per region are not recorded; however, monitoring is performed in the local safety committees within each market area. CEO √Ñlvsbyhus A N N UA L A N D S U S TA I N A B I LI T Y R E P O R T, 2 018 39 PRODU KTOM R√ÖDE N PULPWOOD/CHIPS Record levels of pulpwood The market for pulpwood and chips is very strong and prices have reached record levels. Sveaskog offers a wide range and is a valued partner for paper and pulp mills. P ulpwood is made up of trees and tree parts that cannot be used by the sawmills. The largest volumes of Sveaskog‚Äôs pulpwood come from thinning and regeneration felling. Sveaskog offers a wide range of pulpwood that comes both from its own forest and through the purchase of other forest owners, as well as imports. The offer is also supplemented with cellulose chips from its own sawmill customers. Sveaskog has about 20 pulpwood customers in Sweden. The customers manufacture paper pulp and paper and cardboard that are exported or used in Sweden. The exported pulp is used for packaging and printed cardboard. The pulp is also used in hygiene products such as nappies, paper towels and toilet paper. Pulpwood from Swedish forests has qualities that make it particularly good for packaging with high requirement levels, such as liquid cartons for milk and juice. Sveaskog‚Äôs strength is its extensive experience of working with pulpwood customers, and its focus over recent years on developing goods logistics in partnership with them. Sveaskog also has the advantage of being able to offer a wide range of fresh pulpwood and cellulose chips. A N N UA L A N D S U S TA I N A B I LI T Y R E P O R T, 2 018 47 B IODIVE RSITY AN D NATU R E CONSE RVATION Twenty per cent of the forest is allocated for conservation Sveaskog combines proÔ¨Åtable forestry with the preservation of high natural values. The company decided as early as in 2002 to allocate land for long-term conservation corresponding to 20 per cent of its productive forest land. S veaskog combines proÔ¨Åtable forestry with the preservation of high natural values. The company decided as early as in 2002 to allocate land for long-term conservation corresponding to 20 per cent of its productive forest land. The conservation work uses three different strategies in different geographical scales: eco-parks, conservation forests and consideration for nature in the production forest. The eco-parks There are currently 37 eco-parks across the country, covering a total area of 174,000 hectares. In all eco-parks, at least half the area is allocated for nature conservation, conservation-oriented management and consideration for nature, which in total corresponds to 110,000 hectares. This results in large contiguous forests in landscapes that beneÔ¨Åt species that move over large areas, such as various bird species. Nature conservation forests The nature conservation forests cover a total of 300,000 hectares, varying in size from half a hectare to several hundred hectares. These allocations are spread over the entire country. In the north, most of the conservation forests are left for free development, while in the southern part of the country there is often management to recreate or enhance the natural values. Sveaskog allocates the forest areas with the highest natural values as conservation forests. If a new area of forest worth protecting is discovered, for example when drawing up the inventory prior to logging, this area of forest is swapped with land of a lower natural value, thus ensuring Milestones in Sveaskog‚Äôs1 environmental work Agreement with the Swedish Environmental Protection Agency to Becomes the first Sveaskog give formal protection to Swedish forest Sveaskog is awarded publishes details Restoration/ the company‚Äôs domain company to have the World Wide Fund of its allocated recreation of reserves. Natural value assessments Each year, Sveaskog carries out felling in several thousand locations around Sweden. In all cases, nature valuation inventories are performed before felling in order to pay due regard to the conservation of protected environments and species. All of Sveaskog‚Äôs natural value assessments from 2018 onwards are available at sveaskog.se. The aim of Sveaskog‚Äôs natural value assessment is to Ô¨Ånd structures and elements of importance in conservation terms. It is relatively common for the inventory to show that there are small areas of high natural value in the forest. Sveaskog will then ensure that the substrates required by the species are located both within the assigned Sveaskog‚Äôs eco-parks areas and within the environmentally protected areas THE ECO-PARKS ARE large contiguous areas of countryside left standing during felling. A N N UA L A N D S U S TA I N A B I LI T Y R E P O R T, 2 018 51 CLI MATE The role of the forest in combaing climate change The Swedish forest is of great importance to Sweden‚Äôs aims to become fossil free by 2045. As the forest grows, it helps to take up a large amount of carbon dioxide. By using forest products instead of materials produced using fossil-based resources, we can reduce the negative climate impact. Sveaskog aims to take a leading role in utilising and developing the climatic beneÔ¨Åts that forests provide. T he forest has a crucial impact on the climate. At a time when we need do everything to prevent the Earth's temperature from rising, sustainable use of forests is crucial. Forests and forestry provide beneÔ¨Åts to climate in a number of ways. The growing forest binds carbon dioxide. As Sveaskog fells signiÔ¨Åcantly less than the annual growth, it means that the store of sequestered carbon in the forest is constantly increasing. Part of the felled forest is turned into timber, which then becomes bound in wooden structures. For example, a wooden house can bind the carbon dioxide once taken up by the trees. Using forest raw materials, we can also replace fossil-based products. The more the forest grows, the greater the uptake in some ten years has developed from an innovation of carbon dioxide. Over time, therefore, the greatest project into a full-scale production of raw pine diesel carbon dioxide uptake is in the used forest. Forestry land 2,515 2,460 30 34 In the Sveaskog group, forest assets are recorded divided into growing Growing forest 33,607 32,054 ‚Äì ‚Äì forest, which is recorded as a biological asset at actual value (IAS 41), and Total 36,122 34,514 30 34 forest land, which is recorded at acquisition value. Sveaskog has assessed that there are no relevant market prices that can be used to value forest holdings of the size held by Sveaskog. Sveaskog is thus carrying out a valuation by calculating the current value of expected future cash Ô¨Çows from the growing forest. Valuation at actual value is being carried out based on Valuation Level Three (see Note 26). Cash Ô¨Çows are calculated for the next 100 years ‚Äì a period that is deemed to be the forest‚Äôs felling cycle. Cash Ô¨Çows are calculated on the basis of felling volumes in accordance with Sveaskog‚Äôs current felling plan and assessments of future price and cost developments. Prices are based on a rolling ten-year average (2009-2018). Regarding cost developments, the current normal cost (see model assumptions below) is being applied. InÔ¨Çation assumptions in the model are based on assessed development during the period 2019 to 2119. The cash Ô¨Çows before tax are discounted at an interest rate of 5.75% (5.95), which is deemed to correspond to the long-term weighted average cost of capital (WACC) for this kind of asset. Sveaskog‚Äôs board of directors assesses that this interest rate should describe the long-term cost of capital for an investment in forest assets and is not affected by short-term variations in market interest rates. Accounting with regard to Ô¨Ånancial instruments On the assets side, Ô¨Ånancial instruments recorded in the balance sheet include liquid resources/assets, trade debtors, shares, loans and bonds receivable. Liabilities and equity include trade creditors, loan liabilities and derivatives, long-term liabilities and interest-bearing longand short-term liabilities. Financial instruments are initially recorded at acquisition value corresponding to the instrument‚Äôs actual value via the proÔ¨Åt/loss statement, with additions for transaction costs for all Ô¨Ånancial instruments other than those belonging to the category Financial asset recorded at actual value via the proÔ¨Åt/loss statement. Accounting takes place accordingly, depending on how they have been classiÔ¨Åed as below. A Ô¨Ånancial asset or Ô¨Ånancial liability is recognised in the balance sheet when the company becomes party to the instrument‚Äôs contractual terms. Trade debtors are recognised in the balance sheet when an invoice has been sent. A liability is recognised when the opposite party has performed and there is a contractual obligation to pay, even if the invoice has not yet been received. A Ô¨Ånancial asset is removed from the balance sheet when the rights in the agreement are realised or expire, or when the company loses control of them. The same applies to components of a Ô¨Ånancial asset. A Ô¨Ånancial liability is removed from the balance sheet when the contractual obligation is discharged or otherwise terminated. The same applies to components of a Ô¨Ånancial liability. Acquisition and disposal of Ô¨Ånancial assets are recorded on the business day, which is the day when the company undertakes to acquire or dispose of the asset. At each reporting date the company assesses whether there are objective indications that a Ô¨Ånancial asset or group of Ô¨Ånancial assets are in need of write-down. 102 A N N UA L A N D S U S TA I N A
